<p><b>Graffiti</b> (singular <i><b>graffiti</b></i> or <i><b>graffito</b></i>, the latter only used in <a href="/wiki/Graffito_(archaeology)" title="Graffito (archaeology)">graffiti archeology</a>) is writing or drawings made on a wall or other surface, usually without permission and within public view.<sup id="cite_ref-oxd_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxd-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ahd_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahd-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Graffiti ranges from simple written <a href="/wiki/Moniker_(graffiti)" title="Moniker (graffiti)">"monikers"</a> to elaborate wall paintings, and has existed <a href="/wiki/Graffito_(archaeology)" title="Graffito (archaeology)">since ancient times</a>, with examples dating back to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Graffito_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graffito-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Modern graffiti is a controversial subject. In most countries, marking or painting property without permission is considered <a href="/wiki/Vandalism" title="Vandalism">vandalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Modern graffiti began in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway_nomenclature" title="New York City Subway nomenclature">New York City subway</a> system and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> in the early 1970s and later spread to the rest of the United States and throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology">Etymology</h2></div>
<p>"Graffiti" (usually both singular and plural) and the rare singular form "graffito" are from the Italian word <i>graffiato</i> ("scratched").<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oxd_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxd-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ahd_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahd-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In ancient times graffiti were carved on walls with a sharp object, although sometimes <a href="/wiki/Chalk" title="Chalk">chalk</a> or <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> were used. The word originates from Greek <span title="Greek-language text"><span lang="el">γράφειν</span></span>—<i>graphein</i>—meaning "to write".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Rufus_est_caricature_villa_misteri_Pompeii.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Rufus_est_caricature_villa_misteri_Pompeii.jpg/250px-Rufus_est_caricature_villa_misteri_Pompeii.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Rufus_est_caricature_villa_misteri_Pompeii.jpg/330px-Rufus_est_caricature_villa_misteri_Pompeii.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Rufus_est_caricature_villa_misteri_Pompeii.jpg/500px-Rufus_est_caricature_villa_misteri_Pompeii.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2385" data-file-height="2465" /></a><figcaption>Ancient <a href="/wiki/Pompeii" title="Pompeii">Pompeii</a> graffito <a href="/wiki/Caricature" title="Caricature">caricature</a> of a politician. <a href="/wiki/Villa_of_the_Mysteries" title="Villa of the Mysteries">Villa of the Mysteries</a>.</figcaption></figure> 
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Graffitti,_Castellania,_Malta.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Graffitti%2C_Castellania%2C_Malta.jpeg/250px-Graffitti%2C_Castellania%2C_Malta.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="295" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Graffitti%2C_Castellania%2C_Malta.jpeg/330px-Graffitti%2C_Castellania%2C_Malta.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Graffitti%2C_Castellania%2C_Malta.jpeg/500px-Graffitti%2C_Castellania%2C_Malta.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>Figure graffito, similar to a relief, at <a href="/wiki/Castellania_(Valletta)" title="Castellania (Valletta)">the Castellania, in Valletta</a></figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Prehistoric_graffiti">Prehistoric graffiti</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Megalithic_graffiti_symbols" title="Megalithic graffiti symbols">Megalithic graffiti symbols</a></div>
<p>Most <a href="/wiki/Petroglyph" title="Petroglyph">petroglyphs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoglyph" title="Geoglyph">geoglyphs</a> date between 40,000 and 10,000 years old, the oldest being <a href="/wiki/Cave_paintings" class="mw-redirect" title="Cave paintings">cave paintings</a> in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Paintings in the <a href="/wiki/Chauvet_Cave" title="Chauvet Cave">Chauvet Cave</a> were made 35,000 years ago, but little is known about who made them or why.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Early artists created <a href="/wiki/Stencil_graffiti" title="Stencil graffiti">stencil graffiti</a> of their hands with paint blown through a tube. These stencils may have functioned similarly to a modern-day <a href="/wiki/Tag_(graffiti)" title="Tag (graffiti)">tag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ancient_graffiti">Ancient graffiti</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Roman_graffiti" title="Roman graffiti">Roman graffiti</a></div>
<p>The oldest written graffiti was found in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a> around 2500 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most graffiti from the time was boasts about sexual experiences,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but also includes word games such as the <a href="/wiki/Sator_Square" title="Sator Square">Sator Square</a>, "I was here" type markings, and comments on gladiators.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Graffiti in Ancient Rome was a form of communication, and was generally not considered vandalism.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Certain graffiti was seen as blasphemous and was removed, such as the <a href="/wiki/Alexamenos_graffito" title="Alexamenos graffito">Alexamenos graffito</a>, which may contain one of the earliest depictions of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>. The graffito features a human with the head of a donkey on a cross with the text "Alexamenos worships [his] god."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Medieval_graffiti">Medieval graffiti</h3></div>
<p>The only known source of the <a href="/wiki/Safaitic" title="Safaitic">Safaitic</a> language, an <a href="/wiki/Old_Arabic" title="Old Arabic">ancient form of Arabic</a>, is from graffiti: inscriptions scratched on to the surface of rocks and boulders in the predominantly basalt desert of southern <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, eastern <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>. Safaitic dates from the first century BC to the fourth century AD.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ancient tourists visiting the 5th-century citadel at <a href="/wiki/Sigiriya" title="Sigiriya">Sigiriya</a> in Sri Lanka write their names and commentary over the "mirror wall", adding up to over 1800 individual graffiti produced there between the 6th and 18th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most of the graffiti refer to the frescoes of semi-nude females found there.
</p><p>Among the ancient political graffiti examples were <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> satirist poems. Yazid al-Himyari, an <a href="/wiki/Umayyad" class="mw-redirect" title="Umayyad">Umayyad</a> Arab and <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> poet, was most known for writing his political poetry on the walls between <a href="/wiki/Sistan" title="Sistan">Sajistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a>, manifesting a strong hatred towards the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad" class="mw-redirect" title="Umayyad">Umayyad</a> regime and its <i><a href="/wiki/Wali" title="Wali">walis</a></i>, and people used to read and circulate them very widely.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Graffiti, known as Tacherons, were frequently scratched on Romanesque Scandinavian church walls.<sup id="cite_ref-green_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> artists such as <a href="/wiki/Pinturicchio" title="Pinturicchio">Pinturicchio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">Raphael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Ghirlandaio" title="Domenico Ghirlandaio">Ghirlandaio</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Filippino_Lippi" title="Filippino Lippi">Filippino Lippi</a> descended into the ruins of Nero's <a href="/wiki/Domus_Aurea" title="Domus Aurea">Domus Aurea</a>, they carved or painted their names and returned to initiate the <i><a href="/wiki/Grotesque" title="Grotesque">grottesche</a></i> style of decoration.<sup id="cite_ref-archeology_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archeology-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-atlantic_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 114px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 112px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:AncientgrafS.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Graffiti, Church of the Holy Sepulchre, Jerusalem"><img alt="Graffiti, Church of the Holy Sepulchre, Jerusalem" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/AncientgrafS.jpg/168px-AncientgrafS.jpg" decoding="async" width="112" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/AncientgrafS.jpg/253px-AncientgrafS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/AncientgrafS.jpg/337px-AncientgrafS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="481" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">Graffiti, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">Church of the Holy Sepulchre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a></div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Hagia-sofia-viking.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Viking mercenary graffiti at the Hagia Sophia in Istanbul, Turkey"><img alt="Viking mercenary graffiti at the Hagia Sophia in Istanbul, Turkey" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hagia-sofia-viking.jpg/250px-Hagia-sofia-viking.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hagia-sofia-viking.jpg/500px-Hagia-sofia-viking.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a></span></div>

			<div class="gallerytext">Graffiti on the <a href="/wiki/Sigiriya#Mirror_wall" title="Sigiriya">Mirror Wall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigiriya" title="Sigiriya">Sigiriya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a></div>
		</li>
</ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Contemporary_graffiti">Contemporary graffiti</h3></div>
<p>In the 1790s, French soldiers carved their names on monuments during the Napoleonic <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars:_Campaigns_of_1798" class="mw-redirect" title="French Revolutionary Wars: Campaigns of 1798">campaign of Egypt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JinxArtCrimes_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JinxArtCrimes-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>'s survives on one of the columns of the Temple of <a href="/wiki/Poseidon" title="Poseidon">Poseidon</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cape_Sounion" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Sounion">Cape Sounion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Attica" title="Attica">Attica</a>, Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-shanks_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanks-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The oldest known example of <a href="/wiki/Moniker_(graffiti)" title="Moniker (graffiti)">graffiti monikers</a> were found on traincars created by hobos and railworkers since the late 1800s. The Bozo Texino monikers were documented by filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Bill_Daniel_(filmmaker)" title="Bill Daniel (filmmaker)">Bill Daniel</a> in his 2005 film, <i>Who is Bozo Texino?</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-bozo-texino-walker_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bozo-texino-walker-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bozo-texino-film_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bozo-texino-film-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Contemporary graffiti has been seen on landmarks in the US, such as <a href="/wiki/Independence_Rock" title="Independence Rock">Independence Rock</a>, a national landmark along the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Trail" title="Oregon Trail">Oregon Trail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, an inscription on a wall at the fortress of <a href="/wiki/Verdun" title="Verdun">Verdun</a> was seen as an illustration of the US response twice in a generation to the wrongs of the Old World:<sup id="cite_ref-reagan_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reagan-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><div class="poem">
<p>Austin White – Chicago, Ill – 1918<br />
Austin White – Chicago, Ill – 1945<br />
This is the last time I want to write my name here.
</p>
</div></blockquote>
<p>During World War II and for decades after, the phrase "<a href="/wiki/Kilroy_was_here" title="Kilroy was here">Kilroy was here</a>" with an accompanying illustration was widespread throughout the world, due to its use by American troops and ultimately filtering into American popular culture. Shortly after the death of <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Parker" title="Charlie Parker">Charlie Parker</a> (nicknamed "Yardbird" or "Bird"), graffiti began appearing around New York with the words "Bird Lives".<sup id="cite_ref-russel_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russel-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
	<li class="gallerycaption">World War II graffiti</li>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Modern_Graffiti">Modern Graffiti</h3></div>
<p>Modern graffiti style has been heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop culture">hip hop culture</a><sup id="cite_ref-genius-paul-edwards-hiphopbook_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genius-paul-edwards-hiphopbook-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and started with young people in 1960s and 70s in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tag_(graffiti)" title="Tag (graffiti)">Tags</a> were the first form of stylised contemporary graffiti, starting with artists like <a href="/wiki/TAKI_183" title="TAKI 183">TAKI 183</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornbread_(graffiti_artist)" title="Cornbread (graffiti artist)">Cornbread</a>. Later, artists began to paint throw-ups and <a href="/wiki/Piece_(graffiti)" title="Piece (graffiti)">pieces</a> on trains on the sides subway trains.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and eventually moved into the city after the NYC metro began to buy new trains and paint over graffiti.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>While the art had many advocates and appreciators—including the cultural critic <a href="/wiki/Norman_Mailer" title="Norman Mailer">Norman Mailer</a>—others, including New York City mayor <a href="/wiki/Ed_Koch" title="Ed Koch">Ed Koch</a>, considered it to be defacement of public property, and saw it as a form of public blight.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While those who did early modern graffiti called it "writing",  <a href="/wiki/The_Faith_of_Graffiti" title="The Faith of Graffiti">the 1974 essay "The Faith of Graffiti"</a> referred to it using the term "graffiti", which stuck.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An early graffito outside of New York or Philadelphia was the inscription in London reading "<a href="/wiki/Clapton_is_God" title="Clapton is God">Clapton is God</a>" in reference to the guitarist <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>. Creating the cult of the guitar hero, the phrase was spray-painted by an admirer on a wall in <a href="/wiki/Islington" title="Islington">Islington</a>, north London, in the autumn of 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The graffito was captured in a photograph, in which a dog is <a href="/wiki/Urine_marking#Canidae" class="mw-redirect" title="Urine marking">urinating on the wall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Films like <a href="/wiki/Style_Wars" title="Style Wars">Style Wars</a> in the 80s depicting famous writers such as Skeme, <a href="/wiki/DONDI" class="mw-redirect" title="DONDI">Dondi</a>, MinOne, and <a href="/wiki/Zephyr_(artist)" title="Zephyr (artist)">ZEPHYR</a> reinforced graffiti's role within New York's emerging hip-hop culture. Although many officers of the New York City Police Department found this film to be controversial, Style Wars is still recognized as the most prolific film representation of what was going on within the young hip hop culture of the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-labonte_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labonte-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Fab<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>5 Freddy and Futura 2000 took hip hop graffiti to Paris and London as part of the New York City Rap Tour in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-hershk_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hershk-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Commercialization_and_entrance_into_mainstream_pop_culture">Commercialization and entrance into mainstream pop culture</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commercial_graffiti" title="Commercial graffiti">Commercial graffiti</a></div>
<p>With the popularity and legitimization of graffiti has come a level of commercialization. In 2001, computer giant <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> launched an advertising campaign in Chicago and San Francisco which involved people spray painting on sidewalks a <a href="/wiki/Peace_symbol" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace symbol">peace symbol</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Heart_(symbol)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart (symbol)">heart</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Penguin" title="Penguin">penguin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tux_(mascot)" title="Tux (mascot)">Linux mascot</a>), to represent "Peace, Love, and Linux." IBM paid Chicago and San Francisco collectively US$120,000 for punitive damages and clean-up costs.<sup id="cite_ref-guerilla_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guerilla-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wired_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, a similar ad campaign was launched by <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> and executed by its advertising agency in New York, Chicago, Atlanta, Philadelphia, Los Angeles, and Miami, to market its handheld <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PSP</a> gaming system. In <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable#Controversial_advertising_campaigns" title="PlayStation Portable">this campaign</a>, taking notice of the legal problems of the IBM campaign, Sony paid building owners for the rights to paint on their buildings "a collection of dizzy-eyed urban kids playing with the PSP as if it were a skateboard, a paddle, or a rocking horse".<sup id="cite_ref-wired_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Global_movements">Global movements</h2></div>
<p>When graffiti is done as an art form, it often utitlises the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> even in countries where it is not the primary writing system.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> English words are also often used as monikers.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Europe">Europe</h3></div>
<p>Stencil graffiti artists such as <a href="/wiki/Blek_le_Rat" title="Blek le Rat">Blek le Rat</a> existed in Western Europe, especially in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, before the arrival of American graffiti and was associated more with the <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> scene than with hip-hop.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the 1980s, American graffiti and hiphop began to influence the European graffiti scene.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Modern graffiti reached Eastern Europe in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Some of the earliest graffiti exhibitions outside of the USA were in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, The Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Middle_East">Middle East</h3></div>
<p>Graffiti in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> has emerged slowly, with taggers operating in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Gulf countries</a> like <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> or the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>. The major Iranian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Hamshahri" title="Hamshahri">Hamshahri</a></i> has published two articles on illegal writers in the city with photographic coverage of Iranian artist <a href="/wiki/A1one" title="A1one">A1one</a>'s works on Tehran walls. Tokyo-based design magazine, <i>PingMag</i>, has interviewed A1one and featured photographs of his work.<sup id="cite_ref-pinmag_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pinmag-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">Israeli West Bank barrier</a> has become a site for graffiti, reminiscent in this sense of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>. Many writers in Israel come from other places around the globe, such as JUIF from Los Angeles and DEVIONE from London. The religious reference "נ נח נחמ נחמן מאומן" ("<a href="/wiki/Na_Nach_Nachma_Nachman_Meuman" title="Na Nach Nachma Nachman Meuman">Na Nach Nachma Nachman Meuman</a>") is commonly seen in graffiti around Israel.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv,_Israel.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel.jpg/250px-Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel.jpg/330px-Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel.jpg/500px-Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>A graffiti piece by the artist DeDe found in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Graffiti has played an important role within the <a href="/wiki/Street_art" title="Street art">street art</a> scene in the Middle East and North Africa (<a href="/wiki/MENA" class="mw-redirect" title="MENA">MENA</a>), especially following the events of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> of 2011 or the <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudanese Revolution">Sudanese Revolution</a> of 2018/19.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Graffiti is a tool of expression in the context of conflict in the region, allowing people to raise their voices politically and socially. Famous street artist <a href="/wiki/Banksy" title="Banksy">Banksy</a> has had an important effect in the street art scene in the MENA area, especially in <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">Palestine</a> where some of his works are located in the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">West Bank barrier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">Bethlehem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="South_America">South America</h3></div>
<p>South America has a very active graffiti culture, and graffiti are very common in Brazilian cities. This is blamed on the high uneven distribution of income, changing laws, and disenfranchisement.<sup id="cite_ref-manco7_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manco7-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Picha%C3%A7%C3%A3o" title="Pichação">Pichação</a></i> is a form of graffiti found in Brazil, which involves tall characters and is usually used as a form of protest. It contrasts with the more conventionally artistic values of the practitioners of <i>grafite</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-revela_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revela-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Prominent Brazilian writers include <a href="/wiki/OSGEMEOS" title="OSGEMEOS">Os Gêmeos</a>, Boleta, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Rodrigues_da_Silva" title="Francisco Rodrigues da Silva">Nunca</a>, Nina, Speto, Tikka, and T.Freak.<sup id="cite_ref-globo_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globo-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</h3></div>
<p>There are also a large number of graffiti influences in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian</a> countries that mostly come from modern <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a>, such as Malaysia, where graffiti have long been a common sight in Malaysia's capital city, <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>. Since 2010, the country has begun hosting a street festival to encourage all generations and people from all walks of life to enjoy and encourage Malaysian street culture.<sup id="cite_ref-kharbar_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kharbar-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Types">Types</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Graffiti_terminology" class="mw-redirect" title="Graffiti terminology">Graffiti terminology</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tools">Tools</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Spray_paint" title="Spray paint">Spray paint</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marker_pen" title="Marker pen">markers</a> are the main tools used for <a href="/wiki/Tag_(graffiti)" title="Tag (graffiti)">tagging</a>, <a href="/wiki/Throw_up_(graffiti)" title="Throw up (graffiti)">throw ups</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Piece_(graffiti)" title="Piece (graffiti)">pieces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paint_marker" title="Paint marker">Paint markers</a>, paint dabbers, and scratching tools are also used.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some art companies, such as <a href="/wiki/Montana_Colors" title="Montana Colors">Montana Colors</a>, make art supplies specifically for graffiti and street art. Many major cities have graffiti art stores.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
	<li class="gallerycaption">Graffiti making</li>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Stencil_graffiti">Stencil graffiti</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stencil_graffiti" title="Stencil graffiti">Stencil graffiti</a></div>
<p>Stencil graffiti is created by cutting out shapes and designs in a stiff material (such as <a href="/wiki/Corrugated_fiberboard" title="Corrugated fiberboard">cardboard</a> or subject <a href="/wiki/File_folder" title="File folder">folders</a>) to form an overall design or image. The stencil is then placed on the "canvas" gently and with quick, easy strokes of the aerosol can, the image begins to appear on the intended surface. Some of the first examples were created in 1981 by artists <a href="/wiki/Blek_le_Rat" title="Blek le Rat">Blek le Rat</a> in Paris, in 1982 by <a href="/wiki/Jef_Aerosol" class="mw-redirect" title="Jef Aerosol">Jef Aerosol</a> in Tours (France);<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> by 1985 stencils had appeared in other cities including New York City, Sydney, and <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, where they were documented by American photographer Charles Gatewood and Australian photographer Rennie Ellis.<sup id="cite_ref-ellis_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ellis-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Stickers">Stickers</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sticker_art" title="Sticker art">Sticker art</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner span:not(.skin-invert-image):not(.skin-invert):not(.bg-transparent) img{background-color:white}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner span:not(.skin-invert-image):not(.skin-invert):not(.bg-transparent) img{background-color:white}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span class="bg-transparent" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Sticker_art_in_Sydney._2024_1636291.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Sticker_art_in_Sydney._2024_1636291.jpg/250px-Sticker_art_in_Sydney._2024_1636291.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Sticker_art_in_Sydney._2024_1636291.jpg/330px-Sticker_art_in_Sydney._2024_1636291.jpg 1.5x, /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Sticker_art_2024_-_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sticker_art_2024_-_2.jpg/250px-Sticker_art_2024_-_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sticker_art_2024_-_2.jpg/330px-Sticker_art_2024_-_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sticker_art_2024_-_2.jpg/500px-Sticker_art_2024_-_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Two name tag stickers. Sydney, 2024</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Stickers, also known as slaps, are drawn or written on before being put up in public. Stickers that became widely used include the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Label_228" title="Label 228">Label 228</a> and <a href="/wiki/Name_tag" title="Name tag">name tags</a> stickers.<sup id="cite_ref-10_July_2012_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10_July_2012-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2007_Walde_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007_Walde-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Name tag stickers that were printed with the text "Hello my name is", first introduced by C-Line Products in 1959, became widely used in both graffiti and <a href="/wiki/Sticker_art" title="Sticker art">sticker art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2007_Walde_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007_Walde-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Eggshell stickers, which are very difficult to remove, are also frequently used.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Stickers allow artists to put up their art quickly and discreetly, making them a relatively safer option for illegal graffiti.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tags">Tags</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tag_(graffiti)" title="Tag (graffiti)">Tag (graffiti)</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tag_(graffiti)" title="Tag (graffiti)">Tagging</a> is the practice of writing one's "name, initial or logo onto a public surface"<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in a <a href="/wiki/Handstyle" title="Handstyle">handstyle</a> unique to the writer. Tags were the first form of modern graffiti.
</p><p>A number of recent examples of graffiti make use of <a href="/wiki/Hashtags" class="mw-redirect" title="Hashtags">hashtags</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:center;max-width:1310px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize thumbimage" style="overflow:auto"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Densely-tagged parking area in Århus, Denmark"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg/1300px-Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg" decoding="async" width="1300" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg/1950px-Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg/2600px-Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="14127" data-file-height="1800" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Graffiti_i_bagg%C3%A5rd_i_%C3%A5rhus_2c.jpg" title="File:Graffiti i baggård i århus 2c.jpg"> </a></div>Densely-tagged parking area in <a href="/wiki/%C3%85rhus" class="mw-redirect" title="Århus">Århus</a>, Denmark</div></div></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Throw_ups">Throw ups</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Throw_up_(graffiti)" title="Throw up (graffiti)">Throw up (graffiti)</a></div>
<p>Throw ups, or throwies are large, bubble-writing graffiti which aim to be "throw onto" a surface as largely and quickly as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Throw ups can have fills or be "hollow".<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They prioritise minimal negative space<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and consistency or letter space and height.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pieces">Pieces</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Piece_(graffiti)" title="Piece (graffiti)">Piece (graffiti)</a></div>
<p>Pieces are large, elaborate, letter-based graffiti which usually use spray paint or rollers.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pieces often have multi-coloured fills and outlines, and may use highlights, shadows, backgrounds,<sup id="cite_ref-read_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-read-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> extensions, 3D effects,<sup id="cite_ref-read_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-read-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Character_(graffiti)" title="Character (graffiti)">characters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Wildstyle">Wildstyle</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildstyle" title="Wildstyle">Wildstyle</a></div>
<p>Wildstyle is the most complex form of modern graffiti. It can be difficult for those unfamiliar with the art form to read.<sup id="cite_ref-read_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-read-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Wildstyle draws inspiration from <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">calligraphy</a> and has been described as partially abstract.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The term "wildstyle" was popularized by the Wild Style graffiti crew formed by <a href="/wiki/Tracy_168" title="Tracy 168">Tracy 168</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">the Bronx</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-read_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-read-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Modern_experimentation">Modern experimentation</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Knitted_graffiti_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Knitted_graffiti_1.jpg/250px-Knitted_graffiti_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Knitted_graffiti_1.jpg/330px-Knitted_graffiti_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Knitted_graffiti_1.jpg/500px-Knitted_graffiti_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption>Knitted graffiti in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, Washington</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Spiderweb_Yarnbomb_Installation_by_Stephen_Duneier.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Spiderweb_Yarnbomb_Installation_by_Stephen_Duneier.JPG/250px-Spiderweb_Yarnbomb_Installation_by_Stephen_Duneier.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Spiderweb_Yarnbomb_Installation_by_Stephen_Duneier.JPG/330px-Spiderweb_Yarnbomb_Installation_by_Stephen_Duneier.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Spiderweb_Yarnbomb_Installation_by_Stephen_Duneier.JPG/500px-Spiderweb_Yarnbomb_Installation_by_Stephen_Duneier.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Stephen Duneier's Spiderweb Yarnbomb installation hides and highlights previous graffiti.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Modern graffiti art often incorporates additional arts and technologies. For example, <a href="/wiki/Graffiti_Research_Lab" title="Graffiti Research Lab">Graffiti Research Lab</a> has encouraged the use of projected images and magnetic light-emitting diodes (<a href="/wiki/LED_art" title="LED art">throwies</a>) as new media for graffitists. <a href="/wiki/Yarnbombing" class="mw-redirect" title="Yarnbombing">Yarnbombing</a> is another recent form of graffiti. Yarnbombers occasionally target previous graffiti for modification, which had been avoided among the majority of graffitists.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Purpose">Purpose</h2></div>
<p>Theories on the use of graffiti by <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> artists have a history dating back at least to the <a href="/wiki/Asger_Jorn" title="Asger Jorn">Asger Jorn</a>, who in 1962 painting declared in a graffiti-like gesture "the avant-garde won't give up".<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Public_art">Public art</h3></div>
<p>People who appreciate graffiti often believe that it should be on display for everyone in public spaces, not hidden away in a museum or a gallery.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Art should color the streets, not the inside of some building. Graffiti is a form of art that cannot be owned or bought. It does not last forever, it is temporary, yet one of a kind. It is a form of self promotion for the artist that can be displayed anywhere from sidewalks, roofs, subways, building wall, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Art to them is for everyone and should be shown to everyone for free.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Personal_expression">Personal expression</h3></div>
<p>Graffiti is a way of communicating and a way of expressing onesself. It is both art and a functional thing that can warn people of something or inform people of something. However, graffiti is to some people a form of art, but to some a form of vandalism.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> And many graffitists choose to protect their identities and remain anonymous to hinder prosecution.
</p><p>With the commercialization of graffiti (and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> in general), in most cases, even with legally painted "graffiti" art, graffitists tend to choose anonymity. This may be attributed to various reasons or a combination of reasons. Graffiti still remains the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop#Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">one of four hip hop elements</a> that is not considered "performance art" despite the image of the "singing and dancing star" that sells hip hop culture to the mainstream. Being a graphic form of art, it might also be said that many graffitists still fall in the category of the <a href="/wiki/Extraversion_and_introversion#Introversion" title="Extraversion and introversion">introverted archetypal artist</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Banksy" title="Banksy">Banksy</a> is one of the world's most notorious and popular street artists who continues to remain faceless in today's society.<sup id="cite_ref-banksy_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-banksy-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He is known for his political, anti-war stencil art mainly in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, England, but his work may be seen anywhere from Los Angeles to <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>. In the UK, Banksy is the most recognizable icon for this cultural artistic movement and keeps his identity a secret to avoid arrest. Much of Banksy's artwork may be seen around the streets of London and surrounding suburbs, although he has painted pictures throughout the world, including the Middle East, where he has painted on Israel's controversial <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> barrier with satirical images of life on the other side. One depicted a hole in the wall with an idyllic beach, while another shows a mountain landscape on the other side. A number of <a href="/wiki/Art_exhibition" title="Art exhibition">exhibitions</a> also have taken place since 2000, and recent works of art have fetched vast sums of money. Banksy's art is a prime example of the classic controversy: vandalism vs. art. Art supporters endorse his work distributed in urban areas as pieces of art and some councils, such as Bristol and Islington, have officially protected them, while officials of other areas have deemed his work to be vandalism and have removed it.
</p><p>Graffiti artists may become offended if photographs of their art are published in a commercial context without their permission. In March 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finnish</a> graffiti artist Psyke expressed his displeasure at the newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Ilta-Sanomat" title="Ilta-Sanomat">Ilta-Sanomat</a></i> publishing a photograph of a <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_208" title="Peugeot 208">Peugeot 208</a> in an article about new cars, with his graffiti prominently shown on the background. The artist claims he does not want his art being used in commercial context, not even if he were to receive compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 114.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 112.66666666667px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Mermaid_Sliema.JPG" class="mw-file-description" title="Mermaid in Sliema, Malta"><img alt="Mermaid in Sliema, Malta" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mermaid_Sliema.JPG/169px-Mermaid_Sliema.JPG" decoding="async" width="113" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mermaid_Sliema.JPG/254px-Mermaid_Sliema.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mermaid_Sliema.JPG/339px-Mermaid_Sliema.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2809" data-file-height="2987" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext"><a href="/wiki/Mermaid" title="Mermaid">Mermaid</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sliema" title="Sliema">Sliema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a></div>
		</li>
</ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Territorial">Territorial</h3></div>
<p>Territorial graffiti marks urban neighborhoods with tags and logos to differentiate certain groups from others. These images are meant to show outsiders a stern look at whose turf is whose. The subject matter of gang-related graffiti consists of cryptic <a href="/wiki/Symbols" class="mw-redirect" title="Symbols">symbols</a> and <a href="/wiki/Initials" class="mw-redirect" title="Initials">initials</a> strictly fashioned with unique <a href="/wiki/Calligraphies" class="mw-redirect" title="Calligraphies">calligraphies</a>. Gang members use graffiti to designate membership throughout the gang, to differentiate rivals and associates and, most commonly, to mark borders which are both territorial and ideological.<sup id="cite_ref-ley_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ley-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Radical_and_political">Radical and political</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:M2109_Iraq_War_Protest_(Black_Bloc_Element).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/M2109_Iraq_War_Protest_%28Black_Bloc_Element%29.jpg/250px-M2109_Iraq_War_Protest_%28Black_Bloc_Element%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="153" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/M2109_Iraq_War_Protest_%28Black_Bloc_Element%29.jpg/500px-M2109_Iraq_War_Protest_%28Black_Bloc_Element%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="499" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Black_bloc" title="Black bloc">Black bloc</a> members spray graffiti on a wall during an <a href="/wiki/Protests_against_the_Iraq_War#March_21,_2009" title="Protests against the Iraq War">Iraq War Protest</a> in Washington, D.C.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Many analysts and art critics see artistic value in some graffiti and recognize it as a form of <a href="/wiki/Public_art" title="Public art">public art</a>. According to many art researchers, particularly in the Netherlands and in Los Angeles graffiti is an effective tool of social <a href="/wiki/Emancipation" title="Emancipation">emancipation</a>, or for the achievement of a political goal.<sup id="cite_ref-thimar_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thimar-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In times of conflict graffiti has offered a means of communication and self-expression for members of these socially, ethnically, or racially divided communities, and has been an effective tool for establishing dialog. The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> was extensively covered by graffiti reflecting social pressures related to the oppressive <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> rule over the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">GDR</a>.
</p><p>Graffiti often has a reputation as part of a subculture that rebels against authority, although the considerations of the practitioners often diverge and can relate to a wide range of attitudes. It can express a political practice and can form just one tool in an array of resistance techniques. One early example includes the <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-punk" title="Anarcho-punk">anarcho-punk</a> band <a href="/wiki/Crass" title="Crass">Crass</a>, who conducted a campaign of stenciling <a href="/wiki/Anti-war" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-war">anti-war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminist</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anti-consumerism" title="Anti-consumerism">anti-consumerist</a> messages throughout the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> system during the late 1970s and early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-souther_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-souther-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, graffiti was a major part of the punk scene. The city was covered in names such as "De Zoot", "Vendex", and "Dr Rat".<sup id="cite_ref-stockho_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stockho-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> To document the graffiti, a punk magazine was started that was called <i>Gallery Anus</i>. So when hip hop came to Europe in the early 1980s, there was already a vibrant graffiti culture.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Anarchy_police.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Anarchy_police.jpg/250px-Anarchy_police.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Anarchy_police.jpg/330px-Anarchy_police.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Anarchy_police.jpg/500px-Anarchy_police.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a><figcaption>Police car graffitied with the anarchist <a href="/wiki/Circle-A" class="mw-redirect" title="Circle-A">circle-A</a> symbol</figcaption></figure>
<p>The student protests and general strike of <a href="/wiki/May_1968_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="May 1968 in France">May 1968</a> saw Paris bedecked in revolutionary, anarchistic, and situationist slogans such as <i>L'ennui est contre-révolutionnaire</i> ("Boredom is counterrevolutionary") and <i>Lisez moins, vivez plus</i> ("Read less, live more"). While not exhaustive, the graffiti gave a sense of the 'millenarian' and rebellious spirit, tempered with a good deal of verbal wit, of the strikers.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224211176">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:220px; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>I think graffiti writing is a way of defining what our generation is like. Excuse the French, we're not a bunch of p---- artists. Traditionally artists have been considered soft and mellow people, a little bit kooky. Maybe we're a little bit more like pirates that way. We defend our territory, whatever space we steal to paint on, we defend it fiercely.
</p>
</blockquote>
<div style="padding-bottom: 0; padding-top: 0.5em"><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—Sandra "Lady Pink" Fabara<sup id="cite_ref-chang_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chang-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>The developments of graffiti art which took place in art galleries and colleges as well as "on the street" or "underground", contributed to the resurfacing in the 1990s of a far more overtly politicized art form in the <a href="/wiki/Subvertising" title="Subvertising">subvertising</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_jamming" title="Culture jamming">culture jamming</a>, or tactical media movements. These movements or styles tend to classify the artists by their relationship to their social and economic contexts, since, in most countries, graffiti art remains illegal in many forms except when using non-permanent paint. Since the 1990s with the rise of <a href="/wiki/Street_Art" class="mw-redirect" title="Street Art">Street Art</a>, a growing number of artists are switching to non-permanent paints and non-traditional forms of painting.<sup id="cite_ref-ziptopia-switch_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ziptopia-switch-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-huffpost-streetart_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffpost-streetart-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Contemporary practitioners, accordingly, have varied and often conflicting practices. Some individuals, such as <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Brener" title="Alexander Brener">Alexander Brener</a>, have used the medium to politicize other art forms, and have used the prison sentences enforced on them as a means of further protest.<sup id="cite_ref-voice_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-voice-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
The practices of anonymous groups and individuals also vary widely, and practitioners by no means always agree with each other's practices. For example, the anti-capitalist art group the <a href="/wiki/Space_Hijackers" title="Space Hijackers">Space Hijackers</a> did a piece in 2004 about the contradiction between the capitalistic elements of Banksy and his use of political <a href="/wiki/Imagery" title="Imagery">imagery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tanyabaxter-Gallery_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tanyabaxter-Gallery-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haynes-banksy_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haynes-banksy-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Berlin human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Irmela_Mensah-Schramm" title="Irmela Mensah-Schramm">Irmela Mensah-Schramm</a> has received global media attention and numerous awards for her 35-year campaign of effacing <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazi</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Far-right_politics" title="Far-right politics">right-wing extremist</a> graffiti throughout Germany, often by altering hate speech in humorous ways.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
